## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: chemical reaction kinetics
**Analysis**: This task models the rate of change of concentration dA/dt in a chemical reaction, where the rate typically depends on the current concentration A through rate laws of various orders, and potentially on time t for non-autonomous systems (e.g., time-varying temperature, photochemistry, or catalytic effects).

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Zero-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 (constant rate, independent of concentration)
- First-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A (rate proportional to concentration)
- Second-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A**2 (rate proportional to square of concentration)
- nth-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 (general power-law rate dependence)
- First-order decay: dA_dt = -c0 * A (exponential decay of concentration)
- Reversible first-order: dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 (first-order with equilibrium offset)
- Mixed-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 * A**2 (competing first and second order)
- Michaelis-Menten type: dA_dt = c0 * A / (c1 + A) (saturation kinetics)
- Time-dependent rate: dA_dt = c0 * A * exp(c1 * t) (rate constant varying with time)
- Autocatalytic: dA_dt = c0 * A * (c1 - A) (logistic-type autocatalysis)
- Power-law with time: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 * t**c2 (diffusion-limited or fractal kinetics)
- Inhibition kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A / (c1 + A)**2 (substrate inhibition)
- Cooperative kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 / (c2 + A**c1) (Hill-type rate law)
- Linear combination: dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 * A**2 + c2 (polynomial rate law with offset)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Negative proportionality to concentration → first-order decay dA_dt = -k*A, characteristic of simple irreversible reactions
- Rate proportional to A*(A0-A) → autocatalytic or reversible bimolecular mechanism with conservation constraint
- Fractional power of concentration A**n with 0<n<1 → fractal kinetics or diffusion-limited reactions on heterogeneous surfaces
- Rate law with explicit time dependence → non-isothermal conditions, photochemical flux variation, or time-dependent catalytic activity
- Rational function of A (numerator/denominator polynomials) → enzyme kinetics or surface-catalyzed reactions following Langmuir-Hinshelwood mechanism
- Sum of terms with different powers of A → parallel reaction pathways with different molecularities
- Product of A and a decaying exponential in t → deactivating catalyst or decaying radical initiator
- Quadratic term A*(c-A) with conservation law → closed system with stoichiometric constraint where total concentration is conserved
- Sign change in dA_dt at specific A value → equilibrium concentration where forward and reverse rates balance
